TI Hidden pseudospin symmetry in the Dirac equation
SO PHYSICAL REVIEW C
LA English
DT Article
AB We found the hidden symmetry of the pseudospin approximation which is inherent in the Dirac equation both for the spherical potential and for the deformed potential with axially symmetric shape. For both cases, we found two kinds of conditions, i.e., an exact condition and an approximate condition for the pseudospin symmetry. The former condition is not always satisfied in real nuclei, but the latter condition is realistic and applicable to real nuclei. [S0556-2813(98)50712-1].

TI Pseudospin symmetry in relativistic mean field theory
SO PHYSICAL REVIEW C
LA English
DT Article
ID DEFORMED-NUCLEI; TRANSFORMATION
AB Relating the pseudospin symmetry back to the Dirac equation through the framework of relativistic Hartree-Bogoliubov (RHB) theory, the pseudospin approximation in real nuclei is discussed. From the Dirac equation, the mechanism behind the pseudospin symmetry was studied and the pseudospin symmetry is shown to be connected with the competition between the centrifugal barrier (CB) and the pseudospin orbital potential (PSOP), which is mainly decided by the derivative of the difference between the scalar and vector potentials. With the scalar and vector potentials derived from a self-consistent relativistic Hartree-Bogoliubov calculation, the pseudospin symmetry and its energy dependence in real nuclei is discussed.

TI Temperature dependence of quantal and thermal dampings of the hot giant
   dipole resonance
SO NUCLEAR PHYSICS A
LA English
DT Article
DE single-particle levels and strength functions; thermal and statistical
   models; giant resonances
ID RANDOM-PHASE APPROXIMATION; HIGHLY EXCITED NUCLEI; ROTATING NUCLEI;
   FINITE-TEMPERATURE; COLLECTIVE STATES; SHAPE TRANSITIONS; SPHERICAL
   NUCLEI; LANDAU THEORY; WIDTH; FLUCTUATIONS
AB A systematic study of the damping of the giant dipole resonance (GDR) in Zr-90, Sn-120 and Pb-208 as a function of temperature T is performed. The double-time Green function technique is employed to determine the single-particle and GDR dampings. The single-particle energies, obtained in the Woods-Saxon potential for these nuclei, are used in the calculations. The results show that the coupling of collective vibration to the pp and hh excitations, which causes the thermal damping width, is responsible for the enlargement of the total width with increasing temperature up to T approximate to 3 MeV and its saturation at higher temperatures. The quantal width, which arises from the coupling of the collective mode to the ph excitations decreases slowly with increasing temperature. The effect of single-particle damping on the GDR width is small. The results are found in an overall agreement with the experimental data for the GDR width, obtained in the inelastic a scattering and heavy-ion fusion reactions at excitation energies E* less than or equal to 450 MeV. At high excitation energies (E* > 400 MeV) a behavior similar to the transition from zero to ordinary sounds is observed. (C) 1998 Elsevier Science B.V.
C1 RIKEN, Cyclotron Lab, Wako, Saitama 35101, Japan.
RP Dang, ND (reprint author), Saitama Univ, Fac Sci, Dept Phys, Res Bldg,2F,255 Shimo Okubo, Urawa, Saitama 3888570, Japan.

TI Quantal and thermal dampings of giant dipole resonances in Zr-90,
   Sn-120, and Pb-208
SO PHYSICAL REVIEW LETTERS
LA English
DT Article
ID HIGH-EXCITATION ENERGIES; HOT NUCLEI; COLLECTIVE MOTION; EXCITED NUCLEI;
   WIDTH; TEMPERATURE; SATURATION; DEPENDENCE; STATES; SHAPE
AB The damping of the giant dipole resonance (GDR) is studied in Zr-90, Sn-120, and Pb-208 as a function of temperature T. The results show that the coupling of GDR to the pp and hh states is responsible for the increase of the GDR width with increasing T up to 3 MeV and its saturation at higher T. The quantal width, caused by the coupling to ph excitations, decreases slowly with increasing T. An overall agreement is found between the theoretical evaluations and the recent experimental data in heavy-ion fusion reactions and inelastic alpha scattering. At very high T a behavior similar to the transition from zero to ordinary sounds is observed.

TI Nuclear shell model and interacting boson fermion approximation
SO PHYSICS LETTERS B
LA English
DT Article
DE Interacting Boson Fermion Model; OAI mapping; single j-shell; monopole
   pairing; quadrupole-quadrupole; seniority conserving interaction
ID ODD-A NUCLEI; PAIR APPROXIMATION; EXCHANGE TERM
AB The Interacting Boson-Fermion Model (IBFM) hamiltonian is derived starting from the shell-model interaction, by a straightforward extension of the Otsuka, Arima and Iachello mapping procedure to odd-mass systems. Employing a single j-shell model and identical many nucleon systems, systematic studies of spectra giving the comparison in the shell-model, SD pair truncated model and IBFM are carried out: (i) for various proportions of monopole pairing and Q.Q interactions which simulate vibrational-rotational transition; (ii) for a particular combination of these interactions together with the quadrupole pairing interaction, which conserves seniority. (C) 1998 Elsevier Science B.V.
C1 RIKEN, Wako, Saitama 35101, Japan.
   Saitama Univ, Dept Phys, Urawa, Saitama 338, Japan.

TI Possible deviation of the sum of strengths for the double giant dipole
   resonance from the harmonic oscillator limit
SO PHYSICAL REVIEW C
LA English
DT Article
ID HEAVY-ION COLLISIONS; ELECTROMAGNETIC-EXCITATION; STATES; CA-40
AB It is shown that the part of the nuclear Hamiltonian which contains the products of pp and hh pair operators (the scattering terms) and which has been usually neglected in the calculations of the giant dipole resonance turns out to be definitely important in the study of the double giant dipole resonance (DGDR). The complete energy-weighted sum of strengths (EWSS) for the DGDR and a possible deviation from its value in the harmonic oscillators' limit are derived for the first time with the full nuclear Hamiltonian taken into account. The numerical calculations within a schematic model show an example where this deviation turns to a strong enhancement of the EWSS for the DGDR at various particle numbers.

TI Spreading of the Gamow-Teller resonance in Nb-90 and Bi-208
SO PHYSICAL REVIEW LETTERS
LA English
DT Article
ID NUCLEI; TRANSITIONS; EXCITATIONS; DECAY; SPIN; RPA
AB Spreading properties of the Gamow-Teller resonance in Nb-90 and Bi-208 are Studied within an approach including the 2p2h configuration mixing and the ground-state correlations beyond the random-phase approximation. The M3Y interaction and single-particle wave functions within the standard harmonic oscillator potential are used in numerical calculations. The single-particle energies around the Fermi surface are replaced with the empirical values or those given by a Woods-Saxon potential. Results obtained provide a reasonable account for recent experimental findings. The extension of the present approach to hot nuclei is also provided.

TI Study of the Gamow-Teller resonance in Nb-90 and Bi-208
SO NUCLEAR PHYSICS A
LA English
DT Article
DE giant resonance; spreading width; quenching of Gamow-Teller resonance;
   random-phase approximation; 2p2h configuration mixing; (p,n) reaction
ID SPHERICAL NUCLEI; STRENGTH; RPA; APPROXIMATION; FLUCTUATIONS;
   TRANSITIONS; EXCITATIONS; ESCAPE; DECAY; MODEL
AB An approach is proposed for studying the spreading properties of the Gamow-Teller resonance (GTR) in heavy nuclei including the coupling to 2p2h configurations and the ground-state correlations beyond RPA. The GTR is generated by a proton p-neutron h (pi p-nu h) phonon within the renormalized RPA. The second-order configuration mixing beyond RPA is realized by constructing two-phonon configurations, in which one of two intermediate phonon states is a pi p-nu h phonon. The numerical calculations are performed in the parent nuclei Zr-90 and Pb-208 making use of M3Y nucleon-nucleon interaction and the single-particle wave functions obtained in the standard harmonic oscillator potential, The single-particle energies around the Fermi surface are substituted with the empirical values or those given by a Woods-Saxon potential. The results obtained provide a reasonable account for recent experimental findings on the GTR in these nuclei. The extension of the present approach to highly excited (hot) nuclei is also provided. The GTR is found to be stable against temperatures up to T = 6 MeV. (C) 1997 Elsevier Science B.V.

TI Possible enhancement of the E1 decay rates of double giant dipole states
SO PHYSICAL REVIEW C
LA English
DT Article
ID HEAVY-ION COLLISIONS; ELECTROMAGNETIC-EXCITATION; RESONANCE; NUCLEI;
   ORDER; CA-40; CHAOS
AB The E1 transitional rates between the double giant dipole resonance (DGDR) states and giant dipole resonance (GDR) ones are studied using the wave functions, which include one-, two-, and many-phonon components. It is shown that there is a possibility for the enhancement of the E1 transition rates from the DGDR states to the GDR ones as compared to the harmonic limit. This enhancement arises from the matrix elements for the El transitions between many-phonon terms of the wave functions, which differ by one E1 phonon.

TI New dynamical SU(3) symmetry in deformed nuclei
SO NUCLEAR PHYSICS A
LA English
DT Article
DE SU(3) symmetry; casimir operator; superdeformation; hyperdeformation;
   highly deformed shape
ID SUPERDEFORMATION
AB We found a classification scheme for the states of superdeformed shells which is based upon a new realization of the group SU(3). This is achieved by expressing the generators of SU(3) in terms of boson operators. In contrast to Elliott's SU(3) case, this new SU(3) scheme has the dual nature of SU(3) x SU(3) and results in a degeneracy of a positive and negative parity levels in a given shell. We extend the new SU(3) scheme to the case of hyperdeformation in the triplicate SU(3) and the highly deformed shell in the six-fold SU(3). (C) 1997 Elsevier Science B.V.

DE Tamm-Dancoff approximation; nuclear rotations; SDI; inverted pairing;
   quadrupole-quadrupole interaction
ID NUCLEAR SHELL-MODEL; SYMMETRIES
AB We present evidence that excitations induced by the quadrupole-quadrupole interaction are equivalent to an inverted surface-delta interaction whose largest multipole-pairing component is attractive and has maximum spin. This technical recognition led one to isolate the system's intrinsic energies from the rest in the laboratory frame, trace the origin of the recently introduced optimum pair description of rotation and derive approximate but accurate analytical expressions of various band energies.

TI Magnetic dipole transitions in superdeformed nuclei
SO PHYSICAL REVIEW C
LA English
DT Article
ID PARITY
AB Magnetic dipole transition matrix elements in superdeformed nuclei are calculated based on an axially symmetrically deformed Nilsson model. Several levels become the candidates to be assigned for the experimental evidence of the superdeformed band in Hg-193 and Tl-193. Although the intrinsic g(K) factors for some levels show slower convergence to the asymptotic limit values, their wave functions show a good revival of L-S coupling scheme at superdeformation. Comparing the experimental data with the renormalized g'(K), we find the pseudospin picture is not suitable for the superdeformed band.

TI Microscopic foundations of the interacting boson Model from the
   shell-model point of view
SO PROGRESS OF THEORETICAL PHYSICS SUPPLEMENT
LA English
DT Article
ID COLLECTIVE NUCLEAR STATES; SENIORITY SCHEME; APPROXIMATION
AB The validity of the essential ingredients of the microscopic formulation of the interacting boson model: (i) truncation of the shell-model or fermion space and (ii) the procedures for mapping the truncated fermion space on to the boson space, is tested over various (spherical, deformed and transitional) regions both in the simplistic single j-shell, identical boson systems and the more realistic multi j-shell, proton-neutron systems depending on the feasibility of such calculations. In the situations where the truncation and mapping procedures fail to reproduce the exact shell-model results, it is demonstrated that renormalization and higher order mapping procedures cure the associated problems, respectively and provide excellent agreements. In addition, a Hamiltonian of the interacting boson-fermion model which is relevant for a study of odd mass nuclei is derived for a single j-shell case in the shell-model framework, which yields results identical to those in the shell-model for the monopole pairing interaction.

TI MICROSCOPIC FOUNDATION OF THE INTERACTING BOSON MODEL
SO NUCLEAR PHYSICS A

ID NUCLEAR SHELL-MODEL; SYSTEMS; STATES
AB A microscopic foundation of the interacting boson model is described. The importance of monopole and quadrupole pairs of nucleons is emphasized. Those pairs are mapped onto the s and d bosons. It is shown that this mapping provides a good approximation in vibrational and transitional nuclei. In appendix, it is shown that the monopole pair of electrons plays possibly an important role in metal clusters.

TI PARITY DOUBLET LEVELS IN SUPERDEFORMATION
SO PHYSICS LETTERS B
LA English
DT Article
ID ALIGNMENT; NUCLEI; LINE
AB The different parity single-particle levels with the asymptotic quantum numbers [N, N, 0]1/2 and [N-1, N-2, 1]1/2 are almost degenerate around delta approximately 0.6. TI QUANTIZATION OF ALIGNMENT AND DIFFERENT PARITY PAIR LEVELS WITH
   OMEGA=1/2
SO NUCLEAR PHYSICS A
LA English
DT Article; Proceedings Paper
CT 21ST INTERNATIONAL SYMP ON RAPIDLY ROTATING NUCLEI
CY OCT 26-30, 1992
CL TOKYO, JAPAN
SP UNIV TOKYO, INST NUCL STUDY, INST PHYS & CHEM RES, JAPAN ATOM ENERGY RES INST, NISHINA MEM FDN & COMMEMORAT ASSOC JAPAN WORLD EXPOSIT
HO UNIV TOKYO, HONGO CAMPUS
ID YRAST LINE; NUCLEI
AB Two different parity single-particle levels with asymptotic quantum numbers [N, N, 0]1/2 and [N - 1, N - 2, 1]1/2 are almost degenerate at superdeformation near the fermi surface for Z = 66 and N = 86 or 112. We found that the effect of the spin-orbit coupling force becomes smaller for these parity doublet levels because of the strongly deformed quadrupole field. Then the L - S coupling scheme is recovered for them, indicating the real spin is responsible for the quantization of alignment. As long as the spin-orbit interaction is negligible, the superdeformed levels can be described by SU(3) group with eight generators and Casimir operator.

TI EOS AND FERMI-LIQUID PROPERTIES IN THE 1/N EXPANSION OF A RELATIVISTIC
   MANY-BODY THEORY
SO NUCLEAR PHYSICS A
LA English
DT Article
ID SIGMA-OMEGA-MODEL; NUCLEAR MAGNETIC-PROPERTIES; HEAVY-ION COLLISIONS;
   FREE FIELD-THEORIES; SUPERNOVA EXPLOSIONS; SYMMETRY BREAKING; RESPONSE
   FUNCTION; HIGH-DENSITIES; NEUTRON STARS; LANDAU GHOST
AB The equation of state (EOS) for cold nuclear and neutron matter is investigated in the framework of relativistic meson-nucleon theory employing the 1/N expansion scheme. It is found that the inclusion of the relativistic Fock and correlation energies leads to a softening of the EOS, bringing the results closer to the empirical body of information on the state of matter at high densities. The resulting properties of quasiparticles are investigated using methods of the Landau-Migdal theory. As applications, neutron-star structure and collective excitations in infinite nuclear matter are discussed.

TI NUCLEAR MOMENTS - CONCLUDING REMARKS
SO HYPERFINE INTERACTIONS
LA English
DT Article; Proceedings Paper
CT Yamada Conference 34 / 9th International Conference on Hyperfine
   Interactions ( HFI-IX )
CY AUG 17-21, 1992
CL TOYONAKA, JAPAN
SP YAMADA SCI FDN
HO OSAKA UNIV, FAC SCI, DEPT PHYS & LAB NUCL STUDIES
ID EXCHANGE CURRENTS; AXIAL CURRENTS; QUARK-MODEL; TRANSITIONS; STRENGTH
AB Studies of nuclear magnetic moments and nuclear weak interactions discussed in this Conference are reviewed. The importance of configuration mixing and meson exchange currents is examined, and it is emphasized that the second order configuration mixing (tensor correlation) is essential for the understanding of these phenomena. Recent results concerning nuclear quadrupole moments reported in this Conference are also discussed. Finally, the pairing effect in metal clusters is pointed out and the importance of measuring their spins and magnetic moments is mentioned.

TI A PAIRING EFFECT IN GAMMA-SOFT NUCLEI
SO PHYSICS LETTERS B
LA English
DT Article
ID INTERACTING BOSONS; EVEN NUCLEI; SHELL-MODEL; INERTIA; MOMENT; STATES;
   BANDS
AB A new regularity in the level structure of gamma-soft nuclei is suggested by using the O(6) limit of the interacting boson model. This regularity, which will bc referred to as tau-compression, is thc compression of level spacing between neighboring O(5) multiplets for higher tau-values. It is shown that the pairing interaction is the origin of the tau-compression. The spectra of Xe-126-130 are discussed as prominent examples of the tau-compression.

TI ELECTROMAGNETIC PROPERTIES OF QUASI-PARTICLES IN A RELATIVISTIC
   MANY-BODY THEORY
SO NUCLEAR PHYSICS A
LA English
DT Article
ID SIGMA-OMEGA-MODEL; NUCLEAR-MATTER; MAGNETIC-MOMENTS; FINITE NUCLEI;
   RESPONSE FUNCTION; MATRIX-ELEMENTS; CHIRAL SYMMETRY; FIELD-THEORIES;
   APPROXIMATION; CURRENTS
AB Using a relativistic meson-nucleon theory we describe both the ground state of nuclear matter and the electromagnetic current of a quasiparticle including vacuum fluctuation effects in the same framework. The energy density of nuclear matter is calculated in the two-loop approximation including also those higher-order effects which are known to be essential for stability, and the quasiparticle current is calculated in the one-loop approximation. Due to the consistency between the description of the strong and electromagnetic interactions, all requirements of gauge invariance can be satisfied. Relativistic corrections to thc magnetic g-factors are studied in detail.

TI GINOCCHIO MODEL WITH ISOSPIN
SO PHYSICS LETTERS B
LA English
DT Article
ID DYNAMICAL SYMMETRY MODEL; INTERACTING BOSON MODEL; NUCLEAR SHELL-MODEL;
   FERMION; STATES; LIMIT
AB We study the sp(8) subgroup of the isospin-invariant Ginocchio model. The allowed quantum numbers are determined in terms of Young's diagrams. Using this result, we discuss the excitation energy of a model hamiltonian.

TI EFFECTS OF VALENCE NUCLEON ORBITS AND CHARGE SYMMETRY-BREAKING
   INTERACTION ON THE NOLEN-SCHIFFER ANOMALY OF MIRROR NUCLEI
SO NUCLEAR PHYSICS A
LA English
DT Article
ID COULOMB DISPLACEMENT ENERGY; MAGNETIC FORM-FACTORS; ELECTRON-SCATTERING;
   COUPLING-CONSTANTS; CORE-POLARIZATION; PARAMETERS; ASYMMETRY; FORCES;
   COMPILATION; PB-207
AB Coulomb energy differences (Nolen-Schiffer anomalies) of mirror nuclei O-17-F-17 and Ca-41-Sc-41              Sc are studied by using realistic Hartree-Fock and Woods-Saxon single-particle wave functions which are determined precisely through the analysis of the magnetic form factors of electron scattering. These single-particle wave functions are used to evaluate the Coulomb energy differences due to charge symmetry breaking forces, with new coupling constants determined by the analysis of the scattering lengths of pp and nn system which have been successfully applied to the Coulomb energy difference of He-3-H-3. We also evaluated the effects of the charge symmetry breaking forces using Hartree-Fock wave functions. Together with various other contributions, our calculated values of the Coulomb energy differences, which showed deviations of 3-9% from the experimental values in the previous analysis of Nolen and Schiffer, agree with the experimental values within 1% (2%) accuracy for A = 17 (41).

TI LANDAU GHOST AND THE KALLEN LEHMANN REPRESENTATION IN THE RELATIVISTIC
   MANY-BODY PROBLEM
SO NUCLEAR PHYSICS A
LA English
DT Article
ID INELASTIC ELECTRON-SCATTERING; SIGMA-OMEGA-MODEL; COULOMB SUM-RULE;
   VACUUM POLARIZATION; RESPONSE FUNCTION; FINITE NUCLEI; DIRAC SEA;
   MATTER; FE-56; MESON
AB We extend a method proposed by Redmond for the elimination of the Landau ghost in meson propagators to meson-nucleon field theories at finite density.  This method is based on the perturbative calculation under the requirement of the correct analytic properties of the propagators expressed by the Kallen-Lehmann representation.  Using the dispersion relation technique based on the general framework of perturbation theory, the analytic structure of the meson propagators is clarified, and it is proved that the modified propagators obtained by our method are in fact free of the Landau ghost.  We also construct the effective action incorporating our ghost free propagators and obtain the modified energy density of nuclear matter.  Examples in the 1-loop case are presented.
   As an application, we derive the electromagnetic response function from our modified effective action, employing the generalized vector meson dominance principle.  The RPA Coulomb response function using the ghost free meson propagators is calculated in nuclear matter and the effects of the ghost elimination are discussed.

TI QUARK EXCHANGE CURRENTS IN NUCLEI - EFFECTIVE OPERATOR DESCRIPTION
SO NUCLEAR PHYSICS A
LA English
DT Article
ID SHORT-RANGE PART; DEUTERON THRESHOLD ELECTRODISINTEGRATION;
   ELECTROMAGNETIC FORM-FACTORS; BARYON-BARYON INTERACTION; CLUSTER MODEL;
   ELECTRON-SCATTERING; MAGNETIC-MOMENTS; REPULSIVE CORE; MESON; FREEDOM
AB In this paper we introduce for the first time effective quark exchange current operators which can be used in nuclear structure calculations.  To this end we first solve the equation of motion for a microscopic quark hamiltonian using the quark cluster model.  We then construct the electromagnetic current operator on the quark level, i.e. the photon is coupled directly to the quarks.  By eliminating the quark (internal) degrees of freedom, we derive an effective electromagnetic current operator on the nucleon level.  A part of this effective current corresponds to the conventional impulse and meson exchange currents with vertex factors predicted by the quark model.  In addition, this effective current contains new non-local and isospin-dependent terms which are generated by the Pauli principle on the quark level (quark exchange between nucleons).  When we evaluate these quark exchange currents, we use harmonic-oscillator wave functions as nuclear wave functions including short-range correlations.  We introduce these short-range correlations by solving the Bethe-Goldstone equation with our effective NN potential, which is derived from a microscopic quark hamiltonian.  We investigate the role of these additional quark exchange currents in the magnetic moments and the elastic magnetic form factors of several closed-shell +/- nuclei, such as N-15, O-17, and K-39.

TI SPIN DEPENDENCE OF THE MOMENT OF INERTIA AND THE IBM
SO PHYSICS LETTERS B
LA English
DT Article
ID COLLECTIVE NUCLEAR-STATES; INTERACTING BOSON MODEL; SHELL-MODEL; LIMIT
AB The increase of the moment of inertia observed at high-spin states in deformed nuclei is incorporated into the hamiltonian of the interacting boson model-1 (IBM1) by introducing a new spin-dependent term.  The new hamiltonian suppresses the level spacing at high spins and improves remarkably the description of the level schemes of Er-162, Er-164.  A microscopic origin of this new term is discussed in connection with the pairing correlation by using the OAI method.

AF HOSHINO, T

   ARIMA, A
TI GIANT-RESONANCES OF LIGHT NEUTRON-RICH NUCLEI
SO NUCLEAR PHYSICS A
LA English
DT Article
ID CROSS-SECTIONS
AB A large-scale shell model taking the configuration space up to 3 h-omega is applied to the study of giant dipole resonances of neutron-rich nuclei Li-11 and Be-11.  The dipole states excited by the operator rY1-tau-z are studied in Li-11, while the charge-exchange strengths excited by rY1-tau + 1 and r[Y1-sigma](1)tau + 1 operators are discussed in Be-11.  The strength distributions of these resonances concentrate at much lower excitation energies as compared to the systematics of other nuclei because of the small energy gap between 0p and 0d1s shells.  The giant resonance is predicted at around E(x) = 12 MeV in Li-11 exhausting about half of the sum-rule value.  The low-energy states decoupled from the giant resonance are also found below E(x) = 1 MeV, having a significant fraction of the transition strength, because of the large neutron excess and the loosely bound single-particle state.  The charge-exchange dipole strengths are also found in the energy region E(x) = 5-10 MeV above the ground state of Be-11 having large portion of the sum-rule value.
